1. INTRODUCTION
According to the exploitation plan provided by Claria, it is estimated that 35% of the
material to be extracted from the ground will present a low ore grade, so it will be sent
directly to the disposal areas, while the remaining material will be processed by
plant, and it is estimated that it will have a maximum moisture content of 22%. Later, to
improve workability and capacity, this material will be placed in drying fields until
reach a target humidity of 20% with which it can be sent downstream of the area
of disposal, while, the plant material without humidity reduction, may be
shipped directly in the back (upstream).
For the initial stability analysis of the disposal zone (Reference N°1), and as
first approach,
Test tubes were made in the laboratory adjusting the level of
compaction, fines content and humidity to simulate both materials intended for
deposit. Based on the estimated resistance parameters, an analysis of
stability, thus defining recommendations regarding the level of compaction required,
as well as the maximum inclination allowed for the Neptuno ZD.
With the purpose of validating the initial results and replicating the preparation of the
deposit, during May 2021 a first test embankment (T-01) was built which
Its function was to represent the in situ compaction of the materials in the area, without altering
its moisture content. The resistance parameters estimated at this stage, together with
a reduction in the projected height of the deposit, made it possible to increase the slope of the
zone remaining at 18° for ZD Neptuno (References N°2 and 3). As the third and final part of
validation process, during October and November 2021 two
embankments; (T-02) one to represent the material processed by plant and arranged in the
drying fields (with final humidity 20%), increasing the natural moisture content
of the terrain, and an additional one to represent the sterile material (T-03), maintaining the
natural humidity (17%).
This document exposes the methodology and main results, both of the
construction of the embankments, their geotechnical characterization, as well as
also from the subsequent stability analysis with which they are finally delivered
Recommendations regarding tank geometry and compaction levels
required for the correct performance of the projected slopes.

3. PROJECT BACKGROUND
3.1. LOCATION
The test embankment project is located within the Victoria North ZE, using
the existing forest platforms both for their preparation and for the
temporary stockpile of material. Three platforms can be distinguished in the area (Figure 1), which
were used for the development of the project. Platforms [B] and [C] were used
for the construction of embankments; while Embankments 1 (T-01) and 3 (T-03) were
located on Platform [B], Embankment 2 (T-02); was located in [C]. On the other hand, the
Platform [A] was required for the temporary collection of material from T-01, the
which was disassembled to make room for the T-03. Finally, for all the embankments
built, the manufacturing material was extracted
from the Test Pit within the same area.

3.2. DESCRIPTION
All the embankments were designed with identical geometry, being base prisms
rectangular, and whose cross section has a trapezoidal shape (see Figure 2). the face
The upper part has dimensions of 15 x 6 meters, a total projected height of 2 m and access slopes.
of inclination H:V = 3:1, so that, at its base, the dimensions are equivalent to 27 x 18
meters. The construction of the embankments was carried out using compacted layers, with a
__________________________________________________________________________
Geotechnical Report – Test Embankments and Stability Analysis 3
==================================================================================
PAGE 7
==================================================================================
total of 7 and whose average compacted thickness is approximately 30 cm. The process of
Compaction was carried out by using a smooth roller (T-01 and 02), combined with a roller
goat leg (T-03).
Figure 2. Projected dimensions for the test embankments.
The material used corresponds to that extracted from the eastern slope of the existing test pit in the ZE
North Victoria. The soil with vegetal presence was discarded, which is why a
scarp of the terrain with an approximate thickness of 1.5 meters as shown in Figure 3.
Figure 3. Material extraction process (T-01).
__________________________________________________________________________
Geotechnical Report – Test Embankments and Stability Analysis 4
==================================================================================
PAGE 8
==================================================================================
In accordance with the work procedure (Reference No. 4), the construction process of each
Embankment can be decomposed according to the following:
1. Construction of base layer for leveling the work platform.
2. Transfer of the material required for a layer to a platform.
2.1. Previously, for T-02, material preparation, adding water content
required to achieve the target humidity of 20%.
3. Distribution and compaction of the layer.
4. Layer compaction controls.
5. Repeat steps 1) to 5) until completing the 7 required layers.
6. Execution of 3 pits for extraction of unaltered samples and subsequent execution of
triaxial tests.
7. In-situ pressuremetric test (2) for estimation of soil resistance parameters.
The terrain controls differ between the two terrain campaigns, that is, between the embankment
1 and the two remaining embankments. In the case of these last two we have the following:
For each layer, prior to compaction, the
following controls:
• (2) Modified Proctor Tests
• (2) Granulometry and Atterberg limits
• (8) Humidity controls with laboratory
During the compaction process of each layer, the following were considered:
controls:
• (4) In-situ densities with sand cone after 4 passes of a smooth compaction roller.
• (6) In-situ densities with sand cone after 6 passes of a smooth compaction roller.
• (4) In-situ densities with sand cone after 8 passes of a smooth compaction roller.
On the other hand, for the first embankment, prior to compaction it was considered for each layer,
(1) Modified Proctor and (1) Humidity control with laboratory, and, after
compaction, (4) In-situ densities with sand cone. Additionally, the compaction of
This embankment was made through the combined use of a smooth roller and a goat's foot roller,
estimated weight 11.1 and 11.7 tons, with variable number of passes per layer, being the
usual 2 passes of the knee
or goat's foot, followed by 4 smooth rollers. The detail of the above
It is presented in chapter 4.2 of this report.

4. GROUND CAMPAIGN
The construction of the first embankment took place between May 13 and 25, 2021,
while the following embankments, between October 25 and November 16 of the same
year, all in accordance with the previously described procedure. Additionally, and after the
completion of each embankment, 3 pits were executed in each one (see Figure 4, Left).
with the purpose of extracting unaltered samples for the execution of triaxial UU and
CIU in laboratory. On the other hand, the internal density was estimated at 3 different depths.
situ of the material using a nuclear densimeter (see Figure 4, Right) in order to compare the
results with the traditional sand cone method previously mentioned.
Figure 4. Simplified diagram of pit location (T-01, 02, 03) and density controls with
nuclear densimeter (T-02, 03).
As previously mentioned, the field campaign consisted of both tests
preliminaries to characterize the material, construction of the embankments, compaction and
field control thereof, as well as extraction of unaltered samples and
pressuremetric tests. The results of each of the previous points are presented in
the following paragraphs of the document.
4.1. SOIL PROPERTIES
The material used in the embankments comes from the test pit in the area, however, given the
heterogeneity of this type of soils, differences are observed in embankment 1 with respect to the
two others, mainly associated with the fines content, maximum dry compacted density
(D.M.C.S.) and optimal humidity. Additionally, embankment 1 also has greater
internal variability of these same parameters, while T-02 and T-03 have lower
variability of results both inter-layer, and in general between themselves (inter-
__________________________________________________________________________

==================================================================================
embankment). A summary of the estimated soil parameters is presented in Table 2,
while, between Table 3 and Table 5, the detailed summary per layer for each of the
embankments.

For embankment 1, the material classifies mainly as silty sand (SM), which
locally it is called maicillo, however, and given the heterogeneity in the soils
residuals, samples were also identified as low plasticity silt (ML),
located mainly in the area immediately below the escarpment. This material, present
approximately in the first 2 layers of the embankment, it has a higher content of fines
with greater variability, having an average of 43 ± 7%, while the following layers;
33 ± 2%. Regarding the index properties, no significant variations are observed, which,
for the total of classified samples, the liquid limit (LL) and the plasticity index (PI)
They range between 39 ± 2, and 4 ± 1 respectively. Finally, regarding the D.M.C.S., the two
The first layers show considerable variability, with an average value of 1.87 ±
0.15 g/cm3, while the rest do not have significant variation, estimating a
density of 1.83 ± 0.01 g/cm3.

As for the following embankments, considering the total samples of both, the
fines content ranges on average between 49.5 ± 3%, so that the samples
They are classified according to USCS between silty sands (SM) and low plasticity silts (ML). The
Embankment 3, which represents the sterile material, has a slightly higher fines content
to T-02, which explains that, on average, both the liquid, plastic limit and the index of
plasticity are marginally higher.
On the other hand, regarding the compaction curve, both embankments require, in
average, of the same optimal humidity of 10.5% to develop D.M.C.S., this being
last parameter negligibly lower in the T-03, with an average between both of 1.98
kg/dm3; higher in both cases than the 1.84 kg/dm3 estimated in embankment 1.
Finally, regarding the manufacturing humidity, embankments 1 and 3 simulate the material
sterile, so that the moisture content from the test pit is not modified and
corresponds to the natural humidity of the land. On the other hand, embankment 2 simulates the material
processed in the plant, so the moisture content prior to compaction is
increased. The material, mixed and homogenized for this embankment, reached
satisfactorily the target humidity, developing an average humidity of 19.9 ± 0.8
%, where the coefficient of variation is just 4%, evidencing a correct
homogenization of the material. The construction humidity of this embankment is higher by a
0.7 and 1.6% compared to T-01 and T-03, which have natural humidities of 18.0 and 17.3
respectively. The detail of the manufacturing humidity per layer in each embankment is
presented in Table 6.

4.2. COMPACTION
For embankment 1, it is estimated that the level of compaction achieved, with respect to the D.M.C.S.,
corresponds to 87%, presenting the greatest variability in both inter-layer compactness
as intra-layer. The final moisture content, as for the rest of the embankments,
is higher than the optimum, being in this case 3.8%, however, given that it was only
1 sample taken prior to compaction per layer, said quantity is not enough to be
representative, and it is not possible to correctly estimate the humidity reduction due to the
compaction process where, contrary to what was expected, a slight increase in the
moisture content, a situation that was corrected in the following embankments, where it was
possible to estimate the reduction in moisture content based on the number of passes
compaction. The overall summary of the results by embankment is indicated in Table 7.
Table 7. Compaction summary for each embankment based on sand cones.
T-01 T-02 T-03
D.M.C.S. g/cm3 1.84 2.00 1.97
D.C.S. g/cm3 1.60 1.73 1.86
Modified Proctor % 87.0 86.5 94.4
Packaging Humidity % 18.0 19.9 17.3
Compacted Humidity % 18.4 17.4 15.9
Optimum Humidity % 14.6 10.5 10.5

Embankment 2 also achieves on average a dry density equivalent to 87% of the Proctor
Modified, however, this embankment, compared to the first, has a greater
initial moisture content (+2%), a lower optimal humidity (-4%), and a D.M.C.S.
higher (+9%). This implies that, even though there are differences in the properties of the
material, the compaction method applied here has greater effectiveness, a situation that is
It is also evident when purchasing the T-01 and T-03 embankments, which have humidity
similar initials, both intended to represent sterile material, and with different methods
compaction. The detail by layer of each of the embankments is presented in Table
8 and Table 10.

Embankment 3 was the one that managed to reach a higher level of compactness, with an average of
94% of the D.M.C.S. after 8 passes with a smooth roller. Additionally, and as it was
mentioned, has considerably less variability with respect to its counterpart (T-
01), both inter and intra-layer, which is attributed as a predominant factor to the method of
compaction, where only the smooth roller was used.
Regarding the level of compaction as a function of the number of roller passes, it is
possible to estimate this relationship with the data from embankments 2 and 3, where both
an increase in dry density, such as a decrease in moisture content as
shown in Figure 5 and Figure 6. For embankment 3, whose moisture content was not
modified, the greatest relative increase in density occurs between 4 and 6 passes, being a
slightly less between 6 and 8. While, for embankment 2, both the increase in density,
and moisture loss are practically linear.
Even though a decrease of between 1 to 2% in the moisture content is observed for
both embankments, the initial content is significantly different from the optimal humidity. For
In these last two embankments, it is estimated that said humidity is equivalent to 10.5%, while,
The initial content corresponds to 20 and 17% respectively, so the final humidity
They are approximately 7 and 5% from the optimum.
On the other hand, regarding the level of compaction, it is observed that, for every 2 passes of
additional roller, on average the percentage increase in the D.C.S. corresponds to 1.5% and
0.75% approximately for T-02 and T-03 with respect to the PM. Both for the above, and for
the absolute results of the D.C.S., it is observed that the higher the moisture content of the
terrain the compaction method loses its effectiveness and efficiency, where, between both
embankments, with only a 3% increase in humidity, impacts a decrease
approximately 8% d
and the D.C.S.

estimated density on the unaltered samples in the laboratory, the results obtained by
nuclear densimeter have been discarded, and have not been considered as part of the analysis.

5.2. PRESSUREMETRIC TESTS
In each of the embankments, 2 pressuremetric tests were carried out, at depths
variables between 0.7 to 1.5 m. This type of test differs from triaxial UU tests, firstly
place, given that it corresponds to an in-situ test, and affects a significantly larger area of
soil, also implies a low level of confinement and, finally, both to the direction of
load as in the induced stress path, so that, even when estimating
cut resistance parameters, these should not be considered as homologous to the
estimated in triaxial tests. A typical pressuremetric test curve is presented in the
Figure 10, where a global final loading and unloading phase is identified, as well as
charge-discharge cycles at different pressures.

drained of the entire tank.

7. COMMENTS AND RECOMMENDATIONS
- Regarding the initial project (Reference N°1), that is, the estimates from the
test tubes made in the laboratory, it is observed that for all the embankments the
effective shear resistance parameters are higher than those estimated in said stage
of the project. On the other hand, undrained resistance, both consolidated and unconsolidated
consolidated showed variations with respect to the initial project depending on the level of
confinement, obtaining, in general terms, greater resistance in the embankments
for low confinements, and lower than the initial project for confinements over 30
m soil column.
- Variations in the cut resistance parameters allow, together with the reduction
height of the tank, increase their overall inclination, with a maximum slope of
18° for both sterile and reduced humidity processed material in the Neptuno ZD.
- The undrained resistance (Su) estimated in all embankments, both from tests
U.S.
triaxial and pressuremetric, exceeds the 53 kPa required and defined in the project
initial (Reference N°1) as minimums for the transit of trucks over the warehouse. In
This evaluation considered the use of hopper trucks with a tare weight of 9.7 tons, and weight
combined gross equivalent to 45 tons.
- The embankments reached compaction levels of between 86 and 94% of the D.M.C.S.
Between embankments 2 and 3, where only the moisture content of
manufacturing, a significant impact is observed on the level of compaction, where a
increase of 3% in humidity implies an approximate reduction of 8% of the
D.C.S. On the other hand, regarding embankments 1 and 3, where the method of
compaction and soil properties (% Fines and D.M.C.S.), it is observed that the
degree of compaction achieved for the last embankment exceeds the initial one by 7%
regarding the D.M.C.S. which, in both cases, is not necessarily reflected
significant variations in resistance.
- To define the required compaction level it is possible to resort to tests
CIU triaxials. In them, differences are observed in the behavior of the test specimens.
what g
They have a good relationship with their density (see Figures 15 and 16). The
Higher density samples tend to show predominantly
dilatant, while, in those of lower density, the phase transformation occurs close
to the critical state line, showing little dilatancy, and even, for the sample with lower
__________________________________________________________________________
Geotechnical Report – Test Embankments and Stability Analysis 27
==================================================================================
PAGE 31
==================================================================================
density, a contractive behavior is evident. It is observed that the point of
inflection so that the samples have a predominantly dilatant behavior
corresponds to approximately 85% of the D.M.C.S. Based on the above, and with
based on the compaction levels obtained in the field, it is defined that, for the processing
per plant a D.C.S. will be required. minimum equivalent to 85% of the Modified Proctor,
while, for sterile material, a minimum of 90% will be required.
Figure 16. Trajectories p'-q Tx-CIU tests and % of Modified Proctor. (Left) T-01. (Right) T-03.
Figure 17. Trajectories p'-q Tx-CIU test and % of Modified Proctor for set N°1, in T-02.
- The results using the nuclear densimeter (T-02, T-03) indicate levels of
compaction considerably higher than those estimated using a cone
sand, reaching and exceeding on average 100% of the D.M.C.S., being even
upper in embankment 2, which has a manufacturing humidity greater than T-03. It
above is not consistent with the theory or with the results estimated from the cone
of sand, so its use is not recommended for the control of D.C.S. of the
deposit. Similarly, at the initial stage of the construction of embankment 1 it was
__________________________________________________________________________
Geotechnical Report – Test Embankments and Stability Analysis 28
==================================================================================
PAGE 32
==================================================================================
used an electrical densimeter, which did not obtain good results either, where
In addition, constant calibration is required depending on the characteristics of the soil.
which, given the high heterogeneity in the project's residual soils, makes it difficult
considerably its practical use for density control.
- Regarding the compaction method, although the exclusive use of a smooth roller used
in T-02 and T-03, it is estimated that it achieved higher compaction percentages relative to the
Modified Proctor, this is not necessarily observed to result in an increase
significant in the resistance of the material; while the triaxial tests show
slightly higher shear resistance parameters for the first embankment, the
Pressuremetric tests indicate an equal or greater resistance for embankments 2 and 3.
So, guaranteeing the compaction levels previously defined as
minimums, no clear preference is observed regarding the compaction method,
being able to use exclusively a smooth roller, as well as combined use with a roller
goat leg
- Finally, under the current analysis, the undrained seismic scenario is the one that controls the
tank geometry design. Such evaluation is carried out considering the resistance
not drained and consolidated of the material for the entire deposit. On the other hand, regarding
permanent drained analyses, there is uncertainty regarding the position of the
saturation of the terrain, whose consideration was mentioned in the methodology of this
report. In both cases, the analyzes could be approached from a tensions approach.
effective by incorporating the matrix suction effect that occurs in partially
saturated, as is the case of embankments. The incorporation of this effect implies a
increase in the shear resistance of the soil, which could translate into a modification
of the geometry currently controlled by the temporal situation.

Technical Manager

Triaxial tests
1 Introduction
In this document a series of triaxial tests carried out on unaltered samples are reported.
This report is written at the request of Lancuyen Ingeniería Ltda. It also includes:
granulometry and specific weight of the tested samples.
2 CIU Triaxial Tests
2.1 Test Equipment
The apparatus used for the tests delivered in this report corresponds to a piece of equipment
VJ Tech Dynamic Triaxial System, with a 50kN load frame, actuator
electromechanical, 24 Bit resolution, 50mm diameter sample size, frequency
maximum of 5Hz, and maximum pressure of 2MPa.
The measurements were carried out using the Clisp Studio program – csDYNA Software.
2.2 Results
The tests correspond to undrained consolidated triaxial CIU, in unaltered material. The
material is identified as C1/M1, and C3/M8. The initial data for each sample are indicated in the
Table 1.
For the CIU triaxial test, each sample was previously saturated in three stages: circulation of
carbon dioxide, deaerated water, and increased back pressure. Consolidation was then applied
isotropic, until obtaining a dissipation of excess pore pressure of 98%.
Each cutting test was carried out at a speed of 0.25 mm/min.

Triaxial tests
1 Introduction
In this document a series of triaxial tests carried out on unaltered samples are reported.
This report is written at the request of Lancuyen Ingeniería Ltda. It also includes:
granulometry and specific weight of the tested samples.
2 CIU Triaxial Tests
2.1 Test Equipment
The apparatus used for the tests delivered in this report corresponds to a piece of equipment
VJ Tech Dynamic Triaxial System, with a 50kN load frame, actuator
electromechanical, 24 Bit resolution, 50mm diameter sample size, frequency
maximum of 5Hz, and maximum pressure of 2MPa.
The measurements were carried out using the Clisp Studio program – csDYNA Software.
2.2 Results
The tests correspond to undrained consolidated triaxial CIU, in unaltered material. The
material is identified as C1/M1, and C3/M8. The initial data for each sample are indicated in the
Table 1.
For the CIU triaxial test, each sample was previously saturated in three stages: circulation of
carbon dioxide, deaerated water, and increased back pressure. Consolidation was then applied
isotropic, until obtaining a dissipation of excess pore pressure of 98%.
Each cutting test was carried out at a speed of 0.25 mm/min.

email: iit@udec.cl  www.iit.udec.cl

3. CIU TRIAXIAL TESTS
3.1 Test Equipment
The apparatus used for the tests provided in this report corresponds to a
VJ Tech Dynamic Triaxial System dynamic triaxial equipment, with a load frame of
50kN, electromechanical actuator, 24 Bit resolution, 50mm sample size
diameter, maximum frequency of 5Hz, and maximum pressure of 2MPa.
The measurements were carried out using the Clisp Studio program – csDYNA Software.
3.2 Results
The tests correspond to undrained consolidated triaxial CIU, in material
remolded. The initial data for each sample are indicated in Table 1 and 2.
The samples were prepared according to the results of the test of
Modified Proctor compaction, considering a dry density of 85% of the
maximum dry density (MSD) for the first set of tests (Table 1), and a density
dryness of 87% of the DSM for the second set of tests (Table 2), each
one by one
humidity of 23% and 20%, respectively. The average effective effort of
consolidation for each set was 50, 200, and 450 kPa.
The saturation process was carried out in three stages: carbon dioxide circulation,
deaerated water, and increased back pressure. Consolidation was then applied
isotropic, until obtaining a dissipation of excess pore pressure of 98%.
Each cutting test was carried out at a speed of 0.20 mm/min.
The results are presented based on the following parameters:
Deviatoric stress: 𝑞 =𝜎 −𝜎
(cid:2869) (cid:2871)
Average effective stress: 𝑝(cid:4593) = (cid:2869) (𝜎′ +2𝜎′ )
(cid:2871) (cid:2869) (cid:2871)
∆(cid:3009)
Axial strain: 𝜀 = ∙100% (change in height, divided by height
(cid:3028) (cid:3009)(cid:3290)
